    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Bu" lang="ar">خَلُفَ</orth>
                  </form>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">خَلْفٌ</foreign>, <hi rend="ital">He came after, followed, succeeded,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">remained after, another,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">another that had perished</hi> or <hi rend="ital">died.</hi> (TA.) Hence, in the Kur [vii. 168 and xix. 60], <foreign lang="ar">فَخَلَفَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">مِنْ بَعْدِهِمْ خَلْفٌ</foreign> (TA) <hi rend="ital">And there hath succeeded them,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">come after them,</hi> [<hi rend="ital">a posterity,</hi> or] <hi rend="ital">an evil posterity.</hi> (Bd in xix. 60.) And <foreign lang="ar">خَلَفَهُ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He came after him,</hi> (S, A in art. <foreign lang="ar">دبر</foreign>, Mgh, Msb, TA,) or <hi rend="ital">behind him,</hi> (A ubi suprà, Mgh,) or <hi rend="ital">following him nearly;</hi> (A ubi suprà;) inf. n. as above, (Mgh, TA,) and <foreign lang="ar">خِلْفَةٌ</foreign> also: (Mgh:) or <hi rend="ital">he remained after him:</hi> (K:) and   
      <foreign lang="ar">جَآءَ <ref cref="n11341-1" target="خِلَافَهُ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> likewise signifies [the same as <foreign lang="ar">جآء خَلْفَهُ</foreign>; an inf. n. of <foreign lang="ar">خَالَفَ</foreign> being thus used as an adv. n.; i. e.] <hi rend="ital">he came after him.</hi> (TA.) You say also, <foreign lang="ar">خَلَفَ اللَّيْلُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">النَّهَارَ</foreign>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">خَلْفٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">خِلْفَةٌ</foreign>, <hi rend="ital">The night followed,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">came after, the day.</hi> (MA.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  [Hence,] <foreign lang="ar">خَلَفْتُهُ</foreign>, [aor. as above,] inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">خَلْفٌ</foreign>, [perhaps a mistranscription for <foreign lang="ar">خَلَفَ</foreign>,] <hi rend="ital">I was, after him, a substitute for him:</hi> (TA:) [<hi rend="ital">I supplied his place:</hi> and <hi rend="ital">I superseded him.</hi>] And <foreign lang="ar">خَلَفَهُ</foreign>, (aor. as above, TA,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">خِلَافَةٌ</foreign> (S, Mgh, Msb, K, TA) and <foreign lang="ar">خَلَفٌ</foreign> (TA) and <foreign lang="ar">خِلِّيقَى</foreign>, (S, * K, * TA,) which last is an inf. n. of the intensive kind, (Sgh, MF, TA,) <hi rend="ital">He was,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became, his</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">خَلِيفَة</foreign> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">successor,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">vice-agent,</hi> &amp;c.], (S, Mgh, Msb, K,) or <hi rend="ital">his substitute;</hi> (TA;) <foreign lang="ar">فِى قَوْمِهِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">among,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">in respect of, his people</hi>], (S, TA,) and <foreign lang="ar">أَهْلِهِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">his family</hi>]; relating to good and to evil; wherefore one says, <foreign lang="ar">أَوْصَى لَهُ بِالخِلَافَةِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">he charged him by his will with the being his successor,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">vice-agent,</hi> &amp;c.]; (TA;) or <foreign lang="ar">عَلَى أَهْلِهِ وَمَالِهِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">over his family and his property</hi>]: (Msb:) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n11341-2" target="اختفلهُ" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> signifies the same; (Lh, Ibn-'Abbád, K;) <hi rend="ital">he was,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became, his</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">خَلِيفَة</foreign> (Ibn-'Abbád, TA) <hi rend="ital">after him.</hi> (Ibn-'Abbád, TA.) And <foreign lang="ar">خَلَفَ فُلَانًا</foreign> [alone] <hi rend="ital">He was,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became, the</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">خَلِيفَةٌ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">of such a one among,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">in respect of, his family</hi> (K, TA) <hi rend="ital">and his children.</hi> (TA.) And <foreign lang="ar">خَلَفَهُ رَبُّهُ فِى أَهْلِهِ</foreign> (K, TA) and <foreign lang="ar">وَلَدِهِ</foreign>, (TA,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">خِلَافَةٌ</foreign>, (K,) <hi rend="ital">His Lord was [for him] a</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">خَلِيفَة</foreign> [or <hi rend="ital">supplier of his place] to his family</hi> (K, TA) and <hi rend="ital">his children.</hi> (TA. [In the CK, <foreign lang="ar">اخلف</foreign> is made to signify the same; but this is in consequence of an omission.]) And one says, <foreign lang="ar">خَلَفَ ٱللّٰهُ عَلَيْكَ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">May God be to to thee a</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">خَلِيفَة</foreign> [or <hi rend="ital">supplier of the place</hi>] (S, Msb, K) <hi rend="ital">of thy father;</hi> (S, Msb,) or <hi rend="ital">of the one whom thou hast lost:</hi> (S, Msb, K:) thus one says to one who has lost by death his father (S, Msb, K) or mother (K) or paternal uncle (S, Msb) or any other who cannot be replaced: (Msb, K:) and <foreign lang="ar">خَلَفَ ٱللّٰهُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">عَلَيْكَ خَيْرًا</foreign>, (K,) or <foreign lang="ar">بِخَيْرٍ</foreign>, (AZ, Msb, K,) or both, (L,) and <foreign lang="ar">خَلَفَ ٱللّٰهُ لَكَ بِخَيْرٍ</foreign>, (AZ, Msb,) and <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n11341-3" target="أَخْلَفَ" n="3" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>ٱللّٰهُ عَلَيْكَ خَيْرًا</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">لَكَ خَيْرًا</foreign>: (K: [in which it is implied that these phrases mean <hi rend="ital">May God supply to thee well the place of him whom thou hast lost:</hi> but it is implied in the Msb that the two of them there mentioned mean <hi rend="ital">May God restore to thee good in the place of that which has gone from thee:</hi> and it appears from what here follows that all of these phrases have the latter meaning, whether or not they have the former meaning also:]) to him who has lost property or a child or a thing [of any other kind] of which the replacement may be asked, (S,) or to him of whom that which may be replaced has perished, or died, (K,) one says, <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n11341-4" target="أَخْلَفَ" n="4" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>ٱللّٰهُ عَلَيْكَ</foreign> (S, Msb, K) <hi rend="ital">May God restore to thee the like of that which has gone from thee,</hi> (S, Msb,) or <hi rend="ital">may God restore to thee what has gone from thee;</hi> (K in a later part of the art.;) and <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n11341-5" target="اخلف" n="5" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>اللّٰه لَكَ</foreign>; and <foreign lang="ar">خَلَفَ اللّٰه لك</foreign> : or <foreign lang="ar">خَلَفَ اللّٰه عَلَيْكَ</foreign> is allowable in relation to property and the like; and <foreign lang="ar">يَخْلَفُ</foreign>, like <foreign lang="ar">يَمْنَعُ</foreign> is allowable as its aor., though extr., (K,) as it has no faucial letter to occasion the fet-h: (TA:) and one says also, <foreign lang="ar">خَلَفَ ٱللّٰهُ لَكَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">بِخَيْرٍ</foreign> meaning <hi rend="ital">May God give thee good in the place of that which has gone from thee;</hi> (TA;) and <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n11341-6" target="اخلف" n="6" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>عَلَيْكَ خَيْرًا</foreign>, (Msb, TA,) meaning the same; (TA;) and [so] <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n11341-7" target="اخلف" n="7" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>لَكَ خَيْرًا</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">بِخَيْرٍ</foreign>: and <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n11341-8" target="اخلف" n="8" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>ٱللّٰهُ عَلَيْكَ مَالَكَ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">لَكَ مَالَكَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">May God restore,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">replace, to thee thy property</hi>]. (Msb.) <foreign lang="ar">خَلَفَ أَبَاهُ</foreign>, (K,) aor.

                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">مخلاف</orth>
                  </form> A man <hi rend="ital">who often breaks his promises;</hi> (S, K;) as also   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n11375-1" target="مُخْلِفٌ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n11371"/></foreign>: (TA:) [whence the latter (which properly signifies simply <hi rend="ital">breaking a promise</hi>) is applied to a star, or an asterism, as meaning <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">Unattended with rain:</hi> (see 4:) and in the same sense to clouds (<foreign lang="ar">سَحَاب</foreign>): or, accord. to Freytag's Lex., in this or in the contr. sense.]          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  See also <foreign lang="ar">مُخْلِفٌ</foreign>.          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  And see <foreign lang="ar">مَخْلَفَان</foreign>.       <sense type="A" n="2">-A2-</sense>  Also <hi rend="ital">A</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">كُورَة</foreign> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">province, district,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">region</hi>] (S, Mgh, Msb) <hi rend="ital">pertaining to the people of El-Yemen,</hi> (S,) or in the dial. of <hi rend="ital">El-Yemen;</hi> (Mgh, Msb;) pl. <foreign lang="ar">مَخَالِيفُ</foreign>; (S, Msb;) every <foreign lang="ar">مخلاف</foreign> thereof having a [distinctive] name whereby it is known; (S;) the <foreign lang="ar">مخاليف</foreign> of the people of El-Yemen being like the <foreign lang="ar">أَجْنَد</foreign> of the people of Syria and the <foreign lang="ar">كُوَر</foreign> of the people of El-'Irák and the <foreign lang="ar">رَسَاتِيق</foreign> of the people of El-Jibál and the <foreign lang="ar">طَسَاسِيج</foreign> of the people of El-Ahwáz: (IB:) or <foreign lang="ar">مِخْلَافٌ</foreign> signifies <hi rend="ital">a</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">كُورَة</foreign> (JK, M, K) <hi rend="ital">to which a man comes;</hi> (M;) [<hi rend="ital">in any country;</hi>] and hence the <foreign lang="ar">مخاليف</foreign> of ElYemen, (K,) i. e. its <foreign lang="ar">كُوَر</foreign>: (TA:) some say that there is a <foreign lang="ar">مخلاف</foreign> in every country; (Msb;) so says Khálid Ibn-Jembeh; (TA;) i. e. <hi rend="ital">a</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">نَاحِيَة</foreign> [as meaning a <hi rend="ital">district</hi> &amp;c.]; (Msb;) and thus one says the <foreign lang="ar">مخلاف</foreign> of El-Medeeneh, and of ElYemámeh, (Khálid Ibn-Jembeh, TA,) and the <foreign lang="ar">مخاليف</foreign> of Et-Táïf: (AA, Msb, TA:) but properly it is peculiar to the dial. of El-Yemen. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  Also <hi rend="ital">i. q.</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">بنكرد</foreign> [a foreign word, and perhaps mistranscribed], i. e. The <hi rend="ital">poor-rate</hi> of any particular people or party, which is given by them to [the poor of] their own community: so says Aboo-Mo'ádh: (L:) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n11375-2" target="مَخَالِفُ" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n11377"/></foreign> [is its pl., as also, app., <foreign lang="ar">مَخَالِيفُ</foreign>, agreeably with rule, and] signifies the <hi rend="ital">poor-rates</hi> of the Arabs; (JK, TA;) [as in the saying,] <foreign lang="ar">اُسْتُعْمِلَ فُلَانٌ عَلَى مَخَالِفِ بَنِى</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">فُلَانٍ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Such a one was employed as collector of the poor-rates of the sons of such a one</hi>].
